## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for thermoelastic and thermoplastic constitutive laws describing how a solid’s stress–strain response changes with temperature (e.g., modulus reduction, thermal softening, yielding/hardening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (capturing rapid stiffness change with temperature)
- Polynomial elastic nonlinearity (hyperelastic Taylor form): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinear elasticity in polymers/solids)
- Temperature-dependent nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (nonlinear elastic coefficients depend on T)
- Ludwik / Hollomon-type hardening (strain power law): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic flow with strain hardening; c0 can represent an offset/yield level)
- Thermally softened hardening (separable form): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (hardening in epsilon with multiplicative temperature scaling/softening)
- Thermal softening with bounded factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (c3 + exp(c4 * T)) (stress decreases strongly at high T without diverging)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted-style stress form (phenomenological): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon**c2) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear response)
- Yield-like saturation with hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (approaches a saturation stress with increasing strain)
- Temperature-shifted yield onset (smooth): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (temperature shifts baseline/yield level plus strain hardening toward saturation)
- Critical-temperature transition (e.g., softening/phase change proxy): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) / (c2 + exp(c3 * (T - c4))) (rapid change in apparent stiffness/strength near a transition temperature)
- Coupled cross-term expansion: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (first-order thermo-mechanical coupling/interaction term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification → sigma proportional to epsilon with a T-dependent slope suggests a temperature-dependent modulus E(T) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative factors decreasing with T (e.g., 1/(c0+exp(c*T)) or (c0+c1*T) with negative c1) capture reduced flow stress at elevated temperature.
- Nonlinear elasticity/plasticity onset → inclusion of epsilon**2, epsilon**3, or exp(-c*epsilon) terms often indicates departure from Hookean behavior and gradual yielding.
- Hardening behavior → power-law in epsilon (epsilon**c) or (1-exp(-c*epsilon)) indicates increasing stress with strain but with diminishing increments (concave-down hardening).
- Saturation/plateau stresses → forms like c0 + c1*(1-exp(-c2*epsilon)) encode an upper bound in sigma at large epsilon (common in polymers/foams/limited hardening metals).
- Phase/transition-like temperature effect → logistic-like denominators with exp(c*(T-cT)) represent abrupt property changes near a critical temperature (e.g., glass transition, recrystallization proxy).
- Thermo-mechanical interaction → explicit epsilon*T cross terms indicate coupling where temperature changes the incremental stiffness/hardening rate with strain.
- Avoiding nonphysical divergence at high T → bounded rational/exponential factors prevent sigma from blowing up as T increases, consistent with material softening/melting trends.
- Offset stress level interpretation → additive constants (c0 or c0+c1*T) can represent residual stress, yield stress, or reference stress shifting with temperature.

\[
6.5313\,\epsilon^3\;+\;(-0.6868)T + (0.6868)(289.0808)\;+\;3.0184\,T\log(\epsilon+1)\;-\;3.0184(289.0808)\log(\epsilon+1).
\]
So GT contains:
- a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term (no \(T\)),
- a pure linear-in-\(T\) term (no \(\epsilon\)),
- a \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) interaction term,
- and a \(\log(\epsilon+1)\) term with a constant coefficient (coming from \(-(289.0808)\cdot 3.0184\)).

Any matching candidate must be able to produce **both** \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) and \(\epsilon^3\) and also a standalone linear \(T\) term, with no extra functional forms (exp, sin, rational in \(T\), sqrt(T), etc.) remaining.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*(T - 289.08) + 3.018*(T - 289.08)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*T + 198.6 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 3.018*289.08*log(epsilon+1)`
- `= 6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*T + 198.6 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 872.4*log(epsilon+1)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon^3`
2. `T` (linear)
3. Constant
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)`
5. `log(epsilon+1)`

Note that `T*log(epsilon+1)` can be written as `T*epsilon` only if we approximate, which is forbidden. The key term is `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Let me also note: `T*epsilon` ≠ `T*log(epsilon+1)` — these are fundamentally different functions.

Now I'll check each candidate for the required basis functions.

**Critical observation:** The GT requires both `epsilon^3` AND `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Let me scan for candidates that have both.

Most candidates have `T*c*epsilon` (linear in both T and epsilon) instead of `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These cannot match.

Let me look for candidates with `T*log(epsilon+1)` or equivalent:
- None of the candidates explicitly have `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Wait - let me reconsider. The GT has `c4*(T-c5)*log(epsilon+c6)`. With c5=c3=289.08, this expands to `c4*T*log(epsilon+1) - c4*289.08*log(epsilon+1)`.

No candidate has `T*log(epsilon+1)` as a term. The closest terms involving both T and epsilon are `T*epsilon` (linear product), `T/(epsilon+c)`, etc.

Since `T*log(epsilon+1)` is a fundamentally different basis function from `T*epsilon`, `T*exp(...)`, `T*sin(...)`, etc., and none of the candidates contain this term, none can match.

Let me double-check every candidate systematically for any term involving `T*log(epsilon+...)`:

Scanning all 65 candidates... None contain `T*log(epsilon+c)` as a term.

The closest candidates have `T*c*epsilon` which is NOT equivalent to `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Therefore, no candidate can match the GT, since the essential cross-term `T*log(epsilon+1)` cannot be constructed from any combination of the basis functions present in any candidate.
